הקלה במספר ש"ב להגשה
על ידי קטרינה אדלר בתאריך יום חמישי, 19 יוני 2025,
11:10
סטודנטים יקרים,
עקב המצב אנחנו נבחר 7 הגשות הטובות ביותר, וזאת
משום שאת התרגיל השמיני הגשתם חלקכם תוך כדי
הפצצות, וחלקכם לא הגשתם, מאותן הסיבות.
לגבי תרגילים הבאים, מבקשים שתתחשבו בנו וגם
במורים שלכם לקורס ולא תמרחו אותנו עם בקשות
הארכה כשזה לצורך שיפור ציון ש"ב. תעשו סימולציה
לראות כמה זה ישפר לכם בפועל לציון הסופי. אנחנו
רוצים להעלות פתרונות לטובת הכלל תוך זמן סביר,
במיוחד עכשיו בסוף הסמסטר.
שמרו על עצמכם

[2025-06-29 23:50:34] [ID: false_120363267889904955@g.us_3F11390B3EF098494EBE_12519863259287@lid] פיתי (media content): The image contains a mathematical derivation presented in several numbered steps. The first section shows a derivative formula. The second section explains expanding a function as a geometric series. The third section shows the integration of the resulting series term by term.

Here is the extracted text:

$\frac{d}{d z}[\operatorname{arctanh}(z)]=\frac{1}{1-z^{2}}$.

2. Expand $1 /\left(1-z^{2}\right)$ as a geometric series

For $|z|<1$, we have two back-to-back geometric sums:
$\frac{1}{1-z^{2}}=\sum_{n=0}^{\infty}\left(z^{2}\right)^{n}=\sum_{n=0}^{\infty} z^{2 n}$

3. Integrate term by term

Since the series converges uniformly on compact $|z|<1$, we can integrate from 0 to $z$ :
$\operatorname{arctanh}(z)=\int_{0}^{z} \frac{1}{1-t^{2}} d t=\int_{0}^{z} \sum_{n=0}^{\infty} t^{2 n} d t=\sum_{n=0}^{\infty} \int_{0}^{z} t^{2 n} d t=\sum_{n=0}^{\infty} \frac{z^{2 n+1}}{2 n+1}$

No constant of integration appears because $\operatorname{arctanh}(0)=0$.

Below the title, a "שאלה" (Question) is stated, asking to calculate the arc length of the function $f(x) = \sqrt{1 - x^2}$ on the interval $[0, 1/2]$.
Next, a "פתרון" (Solution) is given, identifying the function as a quarter circle (of the unit circle) in the first quadrant.
The solution is broken down into steps:
"שלב א': נגזור את הפונקציה." (Step A: Differentiate the function.) This is followed by the calculation of the derivative $f'(x)$.
"שלב ב': נחשב את הביטוי שתחת השורש בנוסחת אורך קשת." (Step B: Calculate the expression under the square root in the arc length formula.) This shows the calculation of $1 + [f'(x)]^2$.

Extracted text:
אורך קשת של מעגל
שאלה: חשב את אורך הקשת של הפונקציה $f(x) = \sqrt{1 - x^2}$ בקטע $[0, 1/2]$.
פתרון: זוהי קשת של מעגל היחידה ברביע הראשון.
שלב א': נגזור את הפונקציה.
$f'(x) = \frac{-2x}{2\sqrt{1 - x^2}} = \frac{-x}{\sqrt{1 - x^2}}$
שלב ב': נחשב את הביטוי שתחת השורש בנוסחת אורך קשת.
$1 + [f'(x)]^2 = 1 + \left(\frac{-x}{\sqrt{1 - x^2}}\right)^2 = 1 + \frac{x^2}{1 - x^2} = \frac{1 - x^2 + x^2}{1 - x^2} = \frac{1}{1 - x^2}$
שלב ג': נציב באינטגרל:
$L = \int_{0}^{1/2} \sqrt{\frac{1}{1 - x^2}}dx = \int_{0}^{1/2} \frac{dx}{\sqrt{1 - x^2}}$
פתרון סופי:
$L = [\arcsin x]_{0}^{1/2} = \arcsin(1/2) - \arcsin(0) = \frac{\pi}{6} - 0 = \frac{\pi}{6}$
התוצאה הגיאומטרית, שכן זוהי קשת של 30° (פ/6 רדיאנים) על מעגל היחידה.

There are 5 numbered questions covering various topics in Calculus 2:

1.  A two-part theoretical question:
    a. State Cauchy's criterion for integrals.
    b. Prove it.
2.  Calculate a specific infinite series: Σ (from n=0 to ∞) of 1 / [((e+1)/(e-1))^(2n+1) * (n + 1/2)].
3.  Determine the convergence (absolute, conditional, or divergence) of two improper integrals:
    a. ∫ (from 2 to ∞) of sin(x) / x^p dx.
    b. ∫ (from 0 to π/2) of (x / cos(x)) * sin(tan(x)) dx.
4.  Determine the convergence (absolute, conditional, or uniform) for three functional series:
    a. Σ (from n=1 to ∞) of n^x / x^n.
    b. Σ (from n=1 to ∞) of sin(x*n) / n^x.
    c. Σ (from n=1 to ∞) of (n^x / x^n) * cos(n) * (x^2 / 2^n).
5.  Find the radius of convergence for the power series: Σ (from n=1 to ∞) of (5n^2 + 3n + 5) * n! * x^n.

[2025-07-03 11:12:15] [ID: false_120363267889904955@g.us_3F0D0E30BD2C9CC9262B_181059077582919@lid] פיתי (media content): The file contains lecture notes or a summary about Ordinary Differential Equations (ODEs) in Hebrew.

The content covers various types of ODEs and methods for solving them:

1.  **Basic Definitions:** Defines ODEs, order, degree, initial conditions, general and particular solutions.
2.  **First-Order ODEs:**
    *   Linear ODEs (y' + p(x)y = q(x)) - discusses the integrating factor method.
    *   Bernoulli ODEs - explains the substitution to transform them into linear ODEs.
    *   Separable ODEs - describes the method of separating variables and integrating.
    *   Clairaut's Equation - provides the general and singular solutions.
    *   Homogeneous ODEs (M(x,y)dx + N(x,y)dy = 0 with M, N homogeneous) - lists different substitution methods (y=zx, x=zy) and a specific formula.
    *   Exact ODEs (M(x,y)dx + N(x,y)dy = 0 with ∂M/∂y = ∂N/∂x) - explains how to find the potential function.
    *   Non-Exact ODEs - mentions finding an integrating factor based on specific conditions related to (∂N/∂x - ∂M/∂y)/M or (∂M/∂y - ∂N/∂x)/N.
3.  **Second-Order ODEs (and higher):**
    *   ODEs without the dependent variable y (F(x, y', y") = 0) - suggests the substitution y'=t to reduce order.
    *   ODEs without the independent variable x (F(y, y', y") = 0) - suggests the substitution y'=t and expressing y" in terms of t and dt/dy to reduce order.
4.  **Linear Homogeneous ODEs with Constant Coefficients:**
    *   Explains the characteristic equation (based on the derivative operator D).
    *   Details how to find the roots of the characteristic equation.
    *   Describes how to construct the general solution based on the type (real, complex) and multiplicity of the roots.
5.  **Linear Non-Homogeneous ODEs with Constant Coefficients:**
    *   States that the general solution is the sum of the homogeneous solution and a particular solution.
    *   Focuses on the Method of Undetermined Coefficients for finding a particular solution, providing guidelines for guessing the form of the particular solution based on the form of the non-homogeneous term R(x) (polynomials, exponentials, sines/cosines, and their combinations).
    *   Mentions the "resonance" case where the guess for the particular solution is also a homogeneous solution, requiring multiplication by x or x².
6.  **Cauchy-Euler Equation:**
    *   Explains the method for homogeneous Cauchy-Euler equations using the substitution y = x^r, leading to a characteristic equation for r.
    *   Describes how to form the general solution based on real/complex roots and their multiplicity (involving ln|x| for repeated roots or complex roots).
7.  **Power Series Method:** Briefly outlines the method of assuming a Taylor series solution and solving for the coefficients.

שאלה 2

חברת "גמד לכל אחד" מייצרת גמדי גינה. החברה טוענת שגובהם של גמדי הגינה שהיא מייצרת מתפלג עם ממוצע 50cm וסטיית תקן של 2cm. יואב הוא מעריץ מושבע של גמדי גינה ולכן הוא קנה לביתו משלוח של אלף גמדי גינה. מכיוון שהוא מעריץ של הגמדים הוא החליט למדוד את גובהם של כל הגמדים שהוא קנה והוא גילה שהגובה הממוצע של הגמדים שברשותו הוא 50.1cm. יואב רוצה לתבוע את החברה מכיוון שגמדי הגינה שלהם לא מספיק נמוכים. לשם כך יואב רוצה לבדוק מהו הסיכוי בנתונים של החברה לקבל את התוצאה שהוא קיבל או תוצאה גדולה יותר. ידוע כי התביעה שלו תתקבל אם סיכוי זה קטן מ-5%.

[2025-07-04 15:21:46] [ID: false_120363267889904955@g.us_B337EE7C7496EAA8C1C771FF83B8B3F4_34879546876112@lid] פיתי (media content): This is a comprehensive five-page formula sheet for a probability theory course, authored by "Daniel Grimland (Extended for 2025)". It covers a wide range of topics from basic combinatorics to more advanced concepts like limit theorems and Markov chains.

Here is a breakdown of the contents by section:

### Page 1: Foundations of Combinatorics and Probability

*   **Combinatorics (קומבינטוריקה):**
    *   **Basic Principles:** Sum Rule and Product Rule.
    *   **Coefficients:** Multinomial coefficient.
    *   **Selection Formulas:** A 2x2 table summarizing the four main ways to choose *k* items from *n*: with/without order and with/without replacement (permutations, k-permutations, combinations, and combinations with repetition).
    *   **Binomial Identities:** Newton's binomial theorem and related identities like Pascal's identity.
    *   **Inclusion-Exclusion Principle:** The general formula for the size of a union of sets and a simplified version for symmetric cases.
*   **Probability Spaces (מרחבי הסתברות):**
    *   **Definitions:** Formal definition of a probability space (Ω, F, P).
    *   **Axioms & Properties:** The axioms of probability, including basic properties like the union bound and continuity of probability for nested events.
    *   **Formulas:** Inclusion-Exclusion for probabilities.
    *   **Conditional Probability:** The core definition, the chain rule for intersections, the Law of Total Probability, and Bayes' Theorem.
    *   **Independence:** Definitions for the independence of two events and for mutual independence of multiple events.

### Page 2: Discrete Random Variables

*   **Definitions:** Defines a discrete random variable (RV), its probability mass function (PMF), and conditional random variables (conditioned on an event or another RV).
*   **Independence of RVs:** Defines pairwise and mutual independence for discrete RVs.
*   **Expectation (תוחלת):**
    *   **Definition:** The standard formula for expectation.
    *   **Properties:** Linearity, LOTUS (Law of the Unconscious Statistician), and the product of expectations for independent RVs.
    *   **Key Laws:** Law of Total Expectation (E[X] = E[E[X|Y]]) and the Law of Total Probability for expectation (partitioning the sample space).
*   **Variance and Covariance (שונות ושונות משותפת):**
    *   **Variance:** Defines variance, its properties (e.g., V(aX+b)), and the formula for the variance of a sum of RVs. Includes the Law of Total Variance (V(X) = E[V(X|Y)] + V(E[X|Y])).
    *   **Covariance:** Defines covariance and lists its main properties. Defines uncorrelated variables.

### Page 3: Distributions (Discrete) and Introduction to Continuous RVs

*   **Correlation Coefficient (מקדם המתאם):** Defines the correlation coefficient ρ and its properties, including its range [-1, 1].
*   **Discrete Distributions (התפלגויות בדידות):**
    *   Provides PMFs for several key distributions: Uniform, Bernoulli, Binomial, Poisson, Geometric, and Negative Binomial.
    *   Includes a detailed summary table with the **Mean (תוחלת)**, **Variance (שונות)**, and **Moment-Generating Function (פונקציה יוצרת מומנטים)** for each of these distributions.
    *   Defines the Multinomial distribution and gives its PMF and the covariance between its components.
    *   Mentions the memoryless property of the Geometric distribution.
*   **Introduction to Continuous RVs (משתנים מקריים רציפים):** Begins the formal definition of a continuous random variable using a Cumulative Distribution Function (CDF) and the Borel sigma-algebra.

### Page 4: Continuous Random Variables

*   **CDF and PDF (פונקציית הצטברות וצפיפות):** Defines the Cumulative Distribution Function (CDF) and Probability Density Function (PDF) and their relationship (integral/derivative).
*   **Joint, Marginal, and Conditional Distributions:**
    *   Defines joint and marginal PDFs for multiple continuous RVs.
    *   Defines the conditional PDF (e.g., f(x|y)).
    *   Covers the mixed case (one discrete, one continuous RV).
*   **Expectation and Other Metrics:** States that expectation, variance, and covariance are defined analogously to the discrete case but using integrals instead of sums. Notes that their properties remain the same.
*   **Total Probability/Expectation Analogs:** Provides continuous versions of the law of total probability and law of total expectation.

### Page 5: Distributions (Continuous) and Inequalities

*   **Continuous Distributions (התפלגויות רציפות):**
    *   Provides PDFs and a summary table (Mean, Variance, MGF) for key continuous distributions: Uniform, Exponential, Normal (Gaussian), and Gamma.
    *   **Special Properties:**
        *   **Exponential:** Discusses its memoryless property and its relationship with the Poisson process.
        *   **Normal:** Notes that linear combinations of independent Normal RVs are also Normal.
        *   **Gamma:** Defines it as a sum of independent Exponential RVs.
*   **Inequalities (אי-שוויונים):**
    *   **Markov's Inequality:** For non-negative RVs.
    *   **Chebyshev's Inequality:** Relates deviation from the mean to variance.

### Page 6: Advanced Topics

*   **Moments (מומנטים):**
    *   Defines k-th moments and central moments.
    *   Defines Skewness (צידוד) and Kurtosis (גבנוניות) as the 3rd and 4th central moments, respectively.
    *   **Moment-Generating Function (MGF):** Defines the MGF, its property of generating moments through differentiation, and its relationship with the sum of independent RVs (convolution).
*   **Limit Theorems and Approximations (משפטים חשובים וקירובים):**
    *   **Modes of Convergence:** Defines convergence in probability, almost surely, and in distribution.
    *   **Laws of Large Numbers (LLN):** States the Weak and Strong LLN.
    *   **Central Limit Theorem (CLT):** States the theorem for i.i.d. random variables.
    *   **Continuity Correction:** Mentions the technique for approximating a discrete distribution with a continuous one.
*   **Markov Chains (שרשראות מרקוב):**
    *   **Definitions:** Defines a Markov chain, transition matrix, and state vector.
    *   **Properties:** Describes the evolution of the chain over time (v_n = A^n * v_0).
    *   **Stationary Distribution:** Defines the stationary distribution as the eigenvector corresponding to the eigenvalue 1.
    *   **Techniques:** Mentions solving time-independent problems with linear equations and the "memory extension" technique for higher-order chains.
*   **Useful Taylor Series:** Provides the series for e^x, sin(x), and cos(x).

זורקים 6k קוביות הוגנות. מהו הסיכוי לקבל k פעמים את המספר 6 כאשר:

1. k סופי (בעזרת התפלגות בינומית).
2. k → ∞ (בעזרת משפט הגבול המרכזי). הביעו זאת בעזרת dx - גודל מקטע קטן של פונקציית צפיפות ההסתברות.
3. קבלו בעזרת קירוב סטרלינג, n! = √2πn (n/e)ⁿ, את סעיף 2 מסעיף 1.

### Translation:
**Question 4**

6k fair dice are rolled. What is the probability of getting the number 6 exactly k times when:

1. k is finite (using the binomial distribution).
2. k → ∞ (using the central limit theorem). Express this using dx - the size of a small segment of the probability density function.
3. Using Stirling's approximation, n! = √2πn (n/e)ⁿ, derive the result of section 2 from section 1.
